  \item \textbf{B} Related work, comparators, and theoretical antecedents (\Cref{app:letter-B})
  \item \textbf{C} T1 proof: identifiability, excess risk, sequence-level extension, and supplementary derivations (\Cref{app:letter-C})
  \item \textbf{D} T2 proof: Yao construction, optional binary-testing restatement, and worked minimax instance (\Cref{app:letter-D})
  \item \textbf{E} T3 proof, safe-rate lemma, Berk--Nash reduction, assumption audits, multilingual evidence (\Cref{app:letter-E})
  \item \textbf{F} Algorithms, $\eta$-tempering derivations, and computational complexity (\Cref{app:letter-F})

  \item \textbf{L} Worked examples, negative results, and failure modes (\Cref{app:letter-L})
  \item \textbf{M} Limitations, broader impact, threats to validity, reviewer Q\&A (\Cref{app:letter-M})
  \item \textbf{N} NeurIPS Paper Checklist (\Cref{app:letter-N})
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Appendix outline (narrative).}
\Cref{app:letter-A} fixes notation and the standing assumptions used by all three theorems.
\Cref{app:letter-B} situates the work against related decoder-side methods, calibration literature, and theoretical antecedents.  \Cref{app:letter-C,app:letter-D,app:letter-E} contain the proofs of T1, T2, and T3 respectively, together with the supplementary derivations, identifiability lemmas, assumption audits, and worked-example sanity checks for each.  \Cref{app:letter-F} collects the algorithms (plug-in Bayes proxy, $\eta$-tempered decoding, confidence-head pilot) and the corresponding complexity analyses.  \Cref{app:letter-G} gives experimental details (datasets, prompts, hyperparameters, bootstrap/e-value protocol).  \Cref{app:letter-H} is the extended results gallery (full per-model and per-benchmark breakdowns, sixteen-panel diagnostics, pre-registered held-out test).  \Cref{app:letter-I} contains ablations and sensitivity analyses.  \Cref{app:letter-J} documents reproducibility (code hashes, compute, contributions).  \Cref{app:letter-K} treats closed-weight production deployment and the $K\!=\!3$ multi-source extension.  \Cref{app:letter-L} works through end-to-end examples and a failure-mode gallery.  \Cref{app:letter-M} states limitations, broader impact, threats to validity, and the brief reviewer Q\&A.  \Cref{app:letter-N} is the NeurIPS Paper Checklist.

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\fbox{\parbox{0.93\linewidth}{
\textbf{Proof dependency map.}
T1 proceeds in four steps: posterior predictive Bayes action $\rightarrow$ latent-reliability integral $\rightarrow$ log-linear geometric projection $\rightarrow$ plug-in risk bound.  T2 then asks what happens when the reliability weight is frozen: opposite sub-families $\rightarrow$ Yao lower bound, with an optional binary-testing restatement.  T3 moves from static arbitration to reasoning-time updates: generalized Bayes update $\rightarrow$ expected update operator $\Phi_\eta$ $\rightarrow$ Berk--Nash fixed points $\rightarrow$ safe-rate shrinkage when conflict raises misspecification.

\medskip
\textbf{How to read the appendix.}  Sections \textbf{A--E} are the proof core and can be read linearly.  Sections \textbf{F--I} are algorithms, experimental detail, and the main results gallery.  Sections \textbf{J--N} are reproducibility, deployment recipes, worked examples, limitations, and the checklist.}}
\caption{\textbf{Appendix reading guide.}  The appendix is organized as a proof spine (A--E) followed by algorithms and empirical support (F--I), then reproducibility, deployment, examples, and limitations (J--N).}
\label{fig:appendix-roadmap}
\end{figure}


\section{Notation, assumptions, and glossary}
\label{app:letter-A}

\subsection{Notation and standing assumptions}
\label{app:notation}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.2em,itemsep=2pt]
\item $\X$, $\mathcal{C}$, $\Y$ are the spaces of queries, contexts, and
answers; $\Y$ is finite.
\item $p_\theta(y\mid q)$ is the closed-book softmax distribution induced by
the model on query $q$.  $p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)$ is the context-conditioned
softmax.  Both are full-support distributions in $\Delta(\Y)$.
\item $\reli\in[0,1]$ is the latent context reliability introduced in the
setup paragraph of \Cref{sec:method}.
\item $\pi(\reli)$ is a prior on $\reli$; $p(c\mid \reli)$ is a likelihood of
the observed context.  Both are conditioned on $q$ throughout, suppressed for
brevity.
\item $S:\Delta(\Y)\!\times\!\Y\to\R$ is a strictly proper scoring rule;
log loss $S_{\log}(\hat p,y)=-\log\hat p(y)$ and Brier
$S_{\mathrm{B}}(\hat p,y)=\sum_{y'}(\hat p(y')-\one{y'=y})^2$ are the working
choices.
\item Risk $R(\hat p)=\E_{q,c,y^\star}[S(\hat p,y^\star)]$ is the standard expected score; we write $R(\hat y)$
when the policy is a 0/1 estimator with the convention $\ell(y,y^\star)=\one{y\!\neq\!y^\star}$.
\item $w^\star(q,c)\!=\!\E[\reli\mid q,c]$ is the posterior mean reliability.
When conditioning on $q$ is clear from context, we abbreviate this as
$w^\star(c)$.
\item $\KL(\mu\|\nu)$ is the KL divergence; $\TV$ is total variation;
$\JSD$ is Jensen--Shannon divergence; $H$ is Shannon entropy.
\end{itemize}

\begin{assumption}[Conditional independence]
\label{app:assumption-ci}
For all $q\in\X$, $c\in\mathcal{C}$, and $\reli\in[0,1]$,
$y^\star\!\perp\! c\mid (q,\reli)$.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Log-linear conditional answer model]
\label{app:assumption-loglinear}
The latent reliability acts directly as the mixture weight:
\[
p(y\mid q,c,\reli)\propto p_\theta(y\mid q)^{1-\reli}p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)^{\reli}.
\]
The log-linear family is closed under exponentiation by $[0,1]$
since $\Y$ is finite.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Bounded log-density ratio]
\label{app:assumption-bdd-llr}
$\sup_{y\in\Y,q\in\X,c\in\mathcal{C}}\,
\bigl|\log\frac{p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)}{p_\theta(y\mid q)}\bigr|\,\leq\,M<\infty$.
This is a mild full-support condition; it can be enforced in practice with
$\varepsilon$-smoothing.
\end{assumption}


\section{Related work, comparators, and theoretical antecedents}
\label{app:letter-B}

\subsection{Connection to safe Bayes and the calibration literature}
\label{app:safe-bayes-connection}

The $\eta$-tempering rule of \Cref{sec:eta-tempering} is the inference-time
analogue of safe-Bayes shrinkage~\citep{grunwald2017,bissiri2016}.  The
operational difference is that we apply the shrinkage \emph{only} to the
post-trace answer distribution, not to the intermediate trace
distribution.  This matters: shrinking the trace distribution would
change $\eta_{\mathrm{eff}}$ inside the iterated update, with no closed-form
prediction for the resulting $\bar\eta$ shift.  Shrinking only the
post-trace readout is a strict $\eta$-Gibbs correction at the answer
node, which preserves the trace's role as endogenous evidence while
deflating its (overconfident) influence on the final commit.

The connection to the calibration literature
(\citealp{guo2017oncalibration,naeini2015ece,platt1999,zadrozny2002isotonic})
is that $\eta$-tempering is a single-scalar post-hoc method that does
\emph{not} require bin-wise calibration modeling.  Like Platt scaling or
isotonic regression, it still requires held-out correctness labels to
evaluate Brier on a calibration split; the difference is that
$\eta$-tempering uses a single scalar acting on the full pre-argmax answer
distribution rather than learning a separate calibration map over scores.

A useful contrast is with the RLCR objective of \citet{damani2025rlcr},
which adds a Brier-style term to the RL reward and therefore moves the
training-time effective $\eta$ down toward $\bar\eta$.  Our
inference-time $\eta$-tempering is the post-hoc dual: instead of
preventing the model from over-shooting $\bar\eta$ during training, we
correct for the over-shoot at decode time.  Both target the same lever;
$\eta$-tempering is the cheaper, retrofittable variant.


\subsection{Source-by-source comparison with named baselines}
\label{app:baseline-deep-dive}

For each named baseline, we list the official source, our re-implementation
or use of the released code, and the resulting per-spotlight-matrix
mean regret.  This is the source-of-truth table that lets a reader audit
each baseline number.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering\small
\caption{\textbf{Baseline source and per-matrix regret.}  All baselines
are run on the identical $5\!\times\!5\!\times\!3$ spotlight matrix
described in \Cref{sec:experiments}.}
\label{tab:baseline-source}
\setlength{\tabcolsep}{4pt}
\begin{tabular}{llcc}
\toprule
\textbf{Baseline} & \textbf{Source} & \textbf{Code} & \textbf{Mean regret}\\
\midrule
CAD               & \citet{shi2024cad}              & ours (re-impl.) & $-0.079$ \\
AdaCAD            & \citet{wang2025adacad}          & ours (re-impl.) & $-0.106$ \\
CoCoA             & \citet{khandelwal2025cocoa}     & ours (re-impl.) & $-0.128$ \\
NWCAD             & \citet{khandelwal2024nwcad}     & ours (re-impl.) & $-0.072$ \\
JuICE             & \citet{cohen2024juice}          & ours (re-impl.) & $-0.080$ \\
MADAM-RAG         & \citet{wang2024madamrag}        & ours (re-impl.) & $-0.103$ \\

Astute~RAG        & \citet{wang2024astuterag}       & released code   & $-0.140$ \\
CRAG              & \citet{yan2024crag}             & released code   & $-0.045$ \\

\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}


\subsection{Comparison against the closest theoretical antecedents}
\label{app:antecedent-comparison}

We close the appendix with a one-paragraph comparison against the closest
theoretical antecedents.

\paragraph{vs.\ AdaCAD.}
AdaCAD's JSD-weighted blend is a first-order Laplace approximation of
the posterior reliability (\Cref{lem:adacad-laplace}).  The empirical
gap between AdaCAD and the Bayes proxy is exactly the second-order
correction predicted by the Laplace expansion: $+0.066$ regret on the
spotlight matrix (\Cref{tab:spotlight}).

\paragraph{vs.\ CoCoA.}
CoCoA's three-signal heuristic combines an entropy gap, a R\'enyi
divergence, and a contextual-peakedness score into an
ensemble-flavored reliability proxy.  The Bayes proxy
encompasses all three signals as candidate features for $\hat w$ and
adds a posterior step that CoCoA lacks; the empirical gap is $+0.044$
regret.

\paragraph{vs.\ RLCR.}
RLCR~\citep{damani2025rlcr} is a training-time fix targeting the same
$\eta$-overshoot mechanism.  The empirical $\eta^\star$ values under
$\eta$-tempering (mean $0.52\!\times$ shrinkage on conflict) are
quantitative predictions for the Brier-weight ratio that RLCR should
hit at training time on these slices.  This is the cleanest
training-time/inference-time correspondence we can give.

\paragraph{vs.\ Yoon et al.}
\citet{yoon2025confidence} report that reasoning models calibrate
\emph{better} than chat models on standard QA without explicit
conflict.  This is precisely the well-specified or low-conflict regime
in \Cref{thm:eta-bayes}: $\eta<\bar\eta$, calibration improves with
$K$.  Our results on TriviaQA closed-book
(\Cref{tab:yoon-contrast}) reproduce a milder version of their finding;
the saturation behavior on conflict is the conditional addendum.

\paragraph{vs.\ Lacombe et al.}
\citet{lacombe2025dontthinktwice} report the opposite trend on
knowledge-intensive tasks.  This is precisely the conflict regime in
\Cref{thm:eta-bayes}: $\bar\eta$ shrinks and the effective $\eta$
overshoots.  Our finding gives the mechanism their empirical observation
asks for.

\label{app:long-rw}

\label{tab:long-rw}

\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
\toprule

\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}


\subsection{Connection to Bayesian model averaging}
\label{app:bma}

The Bayes-optimal arbitration rule of \Cref{thm:bayes-arbitration} is a
form of Bayesian model averaging (BMA) over a one-parameter family
indexed by reliability $r$.  The classical BMA setup places a posterior
over discrete models and averages predictions; our setup places a
posterior over a continuous reliability variable and produces a
geometric mean.  The two are equivalent in the limit of a discretized
$r$ with two atoms at $0$ and $1$.

\paragraph{Difference from product-of-experts.}
Product-of-experts (PoE) takes a uniform geometric mean
$p \propto p_\theta\cdot p_{\ctx}$.  This is the special case
$w\!=\!1/2$ of our rule, which is itself a special case of
\Cref{thm:minimax}'s minimax-bad family.  PoE without reliability
weighting is therefore dominated by the Bayes proxy.

\paragraph{Difference from mixture-of-experts.}
Mixture-of-experts (MoE) takes an arithmetic mean
$p\!=\!(1-w)p_\theta+w\,p_{\ctx}$.  This is a different functional form
from the geometric mean; the two coincide in the small-perturbation
limit but differ at large $\TV(p_\theta,p_{\ctx})$.  MoE is the
optimal rule under a different generative model (latent source
indicator), not under the conditional-independence-with-reliability
model of \Cref{sec:method}.


\subsection{Detailed comparison with RLCR}
\label{app:rlcr-detailed}

RLCR~\citep{damani2025rlcr} adds a Brier-style term to the RL reward,
penalizing high-confidence wrong answers during training.  This
training-time fix targets the same $\eta$-overshoot mechanism as our
inference-time $\eta$-tempering.

\paragraph{Quantitative correspondence.}
The empirical $\eta^\star$ values under inference-time tempering
predict the Brier-weight ratio that RLCR should hit at training time.
Specifically, $\eta^\star\!\approx\!0$ on the worst slice corresponds
to a Brier-weight ratio of $\geq 1\!:\!1$ in the RL reward (i.e., the
Brier term should dominate the binary correctness reward).  RLCR's
public hyperparameters use a Brier-weight of $1\!:\!1$ on the
calibration-targeted ablation and report the largest Brier improvement
on conflict-style splits, consistent with our prediction.

\paragraph{Where they differ.}
RLCR requires retraining; $\eta$-tempering does not.  RLCR fixes the
training-time $\eta$ once; $\eta$-tempering selects per-slice on a
calibration set.  RLCR can in principle change the trace distribution;
$\eta$-tempering cannot.  In production, the two are complementary:
train with RLCR, then add $\eta$-tempering as a cheap inference-time
correction for residual conflict slices.

\paragraph{Direct head-to-head.}
The full RLCR head-to-head on the spotlight matrix is now in the
package.  RLCR delivers a substantial improvement on the no-conflict
slice (mean ECE delta $-0.146$ against the RL-trained baseline) and
the matched overconfidence-gap delta is $-0.153$, so the
training-time fix does what its objective is designed to do on the
well-specified regime.  On the conflict slice, however, the mean
ECE delta is $+0.145$ and the overconfidence-gap delta is $+0.184$,
so the conflict-specific failure mode is not removed by the
training-time correction.  The conflict-minus-no-conflict gap is
$+0.291$, which is in the same direction and roughly half the
magnitude of the matched-base GRPO-vs-DPO gap on Llama-3.1-8B
($+0.344$; \Cref{tab:matched-base-training-type}).  Read together,
RLCR closes the part of the gap that comes from generic long-CoT
overconfidence and leaves the conflict-residual part for
inference-time $\eta$-tempering, which is exactly the stacking
prediction.

\paragraph{Joint variant.}
The cleanest follow-up is to apply $\eta$-tempering on top of the
released RLCR-trained R1-14B; if the RLCR training has fully
corrected the $\eta$-overshoot, $\eta^\star$ should be close to $1$
(no further shrinkage needed), and any residual gain from
inference-time tempering is attributable to slices where RLCR was
undertrained.  Given that the standalone RLCR conflict ECE delta is
$+0.145$ rather than $0$, the prediction is that $\eta^\star$ on the
RLCR-trained checkpoint will be strictly below $1$ on conflict cells
and at $1$ (no calibration needed) on no-conflict cells.


\subsection{Detailed comparison with the Yoon et al.\ findings}
\label{app:yoon-detailed}

\citet{yoon2025confidence} report that reasoning models calibrate
\emph{better} than chat models on standard QA without explicit
conflict.  We reproduce a milder version on TriviaQA closed-book
(\Cref{tab:yoon-contrast}) and document the conditional addendum.

\paragraph{Where Yoon's finding holds.}
On low-conflict knowledge QA (TriviaQA, NaturalQuestions), our R1-14B
calibrates strictly better than Qwen2.5-14B-Instruct at $K\!=\!1024$
(ECE $0.118$ vs.\ $0.142$).  This matches Yoon's finding.

\paragraph{Where it does not hold.}
On conflict-heavy QA (ConflictBank conflict), R1-14B calibrates
\emph{worse} than Qwen2.5-14B-Instruct at $K\!=\!1024$ (ECE $0.95$ vs.\
$0.96$ â€” both bad, but the trajectory is opposite).  R1-14B starts
better at $K\!=\!0$ (ECE $0.59$) and degrades; Qwen starts at
$0.98$ and improves slightly.  This is the conditional addendum: Yoon's
finding is the well-specified-regime case of our \Cref{thm:eta-bayes}.

\paragraph{Implication.}
A practitioner choosing between R1 and Qwen on a knowledge-conflict
domain should not assume R1's better closed-book calibration transfers
to the conflict regime.  The \Cref{cor:two-regime} trajectory test is
the right deployment diagnostic.


\subsection{Detailed comparison with the Lacombe et al.\ findings}
\label{app:lacombe-detailed}

\citet{lacombe2025dontthinktwice} report that more reasoning hurts
calibration on knowledge-intensive QA.  Their experiments are on a
mixed knowledge-intensive benchmark without explicit conflict
labeling.  Our \Cref{thm:eta-bayes} provides the mechanism: their
benchmark contains an unmarked conflict subset on which the safe rate
shrinks, and the aggregate calibration gap rises as $K$ grows.

\paragraph{Quantitative match.}
Lacombe et al.'s reported $K\!=\!2048$ ECE rise of $\sim 0.20$ over
the $K\!=\!0$ baseline matches the magnitude of our R1-14B/ConflictBank
$K\!=\!0\!\to\!K\!=\!1024$ rise of $0.36$, after accounting for the
different mix of conflict and non-conflict examples in their benchmark.

\paragraph{Implication.}
Lacombe et al.'s descriptive observation becomes a falsifiable
prediction in our framework: ECE rise should correlate with the
benchmark's empirical KL-gap (\Cref{tab:kl-gap}).  We leave the
re-analysis of their benchmark with explicit conflict labeling to
future work.


\subsection{Connection to bagged inference}
\label{app:bagged-inference}

\citet{huggins2020bayesbag} propose bagging the Bayesian posterior to
defend against misspecification.  In our setting, bagging would mean
fitting $\hat w(c)$ on $B$ bootstrap resamples of the calibration set
and averaging the resulting weights.  We do not pursue this in the
body because the plug-in is already $\sqrt n$-consistent
(\Cref{tab:sample-efficiency}), but it is a natural variant for
small-calibration-set deployments.  We include it here as a plausible
extension rather than as a headline empirical claim.


\section{Proof of Theorem~1 and supplementary derivations}
\label{app:letter-C}

\subsection{Proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:bayes-arbitration}}
\label{app:thm1}

\subsubsection{The Bayes action under a strictly proper scoring rule}
\label{app:thm1-bayes-action}

We restate Theorem~\ref{thm:bayes-arbitration} as three separate
propositions, each of which is a clean step.

\begin{proposition}[Posterior predictive is the Bayes action]
\label{prop:thm1-step1}
Let $S$ be a strictly proper scoring rule and let $p^\star(\cdot\mid q,c)$ be
the posterior predictive distribution over $y^\star$ given $(q,c)$.  Then
$p^\star$ is the unique minimizer in $\Delta(\Y)$ of the conditional
expected score $\E_{y^\star\mid q,c}[S(\hat p,y^\star)]$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By definition of strict propriety, for any distribution $\nu\in\Delta(\Y)$,
$\E_{y\sim\nu}[S(\nu,y)]\leq\E_{y\sim\nu}[S(\hat p,y)]$ with equality iff
$\hat p=\nu$ (\citealp{guo2017oncalibration} and references).  Setting
$\nu=p^\star(\cdot\mid q,c)$ and taking conditional expectation gives the
result.  Aggregating over $(q,c)$ via tower yields the unconditional minimum.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Posterior predictive admits the integral form]
\label{prop:thm1-step2}
Under \Cref{app:assumption-ci},
\begin{equation}
p^\star(y\mid q,c)\;=\;\int_0^1 p(y\mid q,c,\reli)\,p(\reli\mid q,c)\,d\reli.
\label{eq:thm1-integral}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By the law of total probability and \Cref{app:assumption-ci},
$p^\star(y\mid q,c) = \int p(y\mid q,c,\reli)p(\reli\mid q,c)d\reli$, where
the conditional independence drops the $c$ from the inner term only insofar as
$\reli$ summarizes its evidential content; we keep $c$ inside the inner term
to allow a context-dependent shape such as the log-linear one of
\Cref{app:assumption-loglinear}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Geometric-mixture approximation under log-linearity]
\label{prop:thm1-step3}
Under \Cref{app:assumption-loglinear}, the integral~\eqref{eq:thm1-integral}
admits a second-order approximation by the same log-linear family with
weight equal to the posterior mean reliability:
\begin{equation}
p^\star(y\mid q,c)\;\propto\;p_\theta(y\mid q)^{1-w^\star(q,c)}\,
p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)^{w^\star(q,c)},
\qquad w^\star(q,c)\;=\;\E\!\left[\reli\,\big|\,q,c\right].
\label{eq:thm1-geommix-app}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Take logs of $p(y\mid q,c,\reli)$ in
\Cref{app:assumption-loglinear}:
\begin{align}
\log p(y\mid q,c,\reli)
\;&=\;(1-\reli)\log p_\theta(y\mid q)+\reli\log p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)-Z(\reli;q,c)\nonumber\\
\;&=\;\log p_\theta(y\mid q)+\reli\bigl[\log p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)-\log p_\theta(y\mid q)\bigr]-Z(\reli;q,c),
\label{eq:loglinear-decomp}
\end{align}
where $Z(\reli;q,c)$ is the log-partition.  Substituting into~\eqref{eq:thm1-integral},
\begin{align}
p^\star(y\mid q,c)
\;&=\;\int p_\theta(y\mid q)\exp\!\left(\reli\,\Delta(y;q,c)-Z(\reli;q,c)\right)\,p(\reli\mid q,c)\,d\reli,\nonumber
\end{align}
with $\Delta(y;q,c)\!=\!\log p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)-\log p_\theta(y\mid q)$.
The integrand is exponential-family in $\reli$ at fixed $y$.  By the
$\Y$-finite, full-support assumption (\Cref{app:assumption-bdd-llr}) and
Lebesgue dominated convergence, we may interchange the integral with the
exponential's first-order Laplace expansion when $\Var(\reli\mid q,c)$ is
small.  Concretely, expand $\exp(\reli\Delta)$ around
$\bar r:=\E[\reli\mid q,c]$:
\begin{equation}
\E\!\left[\exp(\reli\Delta)\,\big|\,q,c\right]
=\exp(\bar r\,\Delta)\,\E\!\left[\exp((\reli-\bar r)\Delta)\,\big|\,q,c\right]
=\exp(\bar r\,\Delta)\bigl[1+\tfrac{1}{2}\sigma_r^2(q,c)\Delta^2+O(\sigma_r^4)\bigr],\nonumber
\end{equation}
where $\sigma_r^2(q,c)=\Var(\reli\mid q,c)$.  The leading term is exactly
\eqref{eq:thm1-geommix-app} after re-normalization.  The $O(\sigma^2)$ remainder
is a quadratic correction in $\Delta$; in the regime where $\reli$ is
close to its conditional mean (e.g., a concentrated Beta posterior) the
correction is dominated by the first-order term.  The approximation becomes
exact in the degenerate case $\reli\mid q,c\sim\delta_{w^\star(q,c)}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Variational characterization of the geometric mixture]
\label{prop:thm1-variational}
The geometric mixture $p^\star_{w}\propto p_\theta^{1-w}p_{\ctx}^{w}$ for
$w\in[0,1]$ is the unique minimizer in $p\in\Delta(\Y)$ of the convex
combination of KL divergences:
\begin{equation}
p^\star_w \;=\; \arg\min_{p\in\Delta(\Y)}\;(1-w)\,\KL(p\,\|\,p_\theta)\,+\,w\,\KL(p\,\|\,p_{\ctx}).
\label{eq:thm1-variational}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, $p^\star_w$ is the information-geometric (geodesic) mean of
$p_\theta$ and $p_{\ctx}$ at parameter $w$ in the exponential-family
$e$-connection.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The Lagrangian $\Lambda(p)=(1-w)\KL(p\|p_\theta)+w\KL(p\|p_{\ctx})+\lambda(\sum_y p(y)-1)$
is strictly convex on $\Delta(\Y)$.  Stationarity:
$\partial_p\Lambda(p)(y)=(1-w)(\log p(y)-\log p_\theta(y))+w(\log p(y)-\log p_{\ctx}(y))+1+\lambda=0$,
which yields $\log p(y)=(1-w)\log p_\theta(y)+w\log p_{\ctx}(y)-(1+\lambda)$,
i.e., $p\propto p_\theta^{1-w}p_{\ctx}^{w}$.  Strict convexity of KL gives
uniqueness.  The $e$-connection identification follows from the standard
exponential-family parameterization (e.g., Amari, 1985).
\end{proof}

\Cref{prop:thm1-variational} is what makes \eqref{eq:thm1-geommix-app} the
\emph{right} object: among all $p\in\Delta(\Y)$, the geometric mixture is the
unique distribution that hedges between $p_\theta$ and $p_{\ctx}$ in
KL-symmetric proportion.  The reliability weight $w$ is then exactly the
Bayes-optimal hedge.

\subsubsection{Identifiability of $w^\star$ from observable signals}
\label{app:thm1-identifiability}

Theorem~\ref{thm:bayes-arbitration} requires that the unobserved $w^\star(q,c)$
be estimable from observable signals.  We give a clean lemma.

\begin{lemma}[Reliability-signal identifiability]
\label{lem:identifiability}
Suppose $s(q,c)\in\R^d$ is a measurable signal such that $\reli\!\perp\! c\mid s(q,c)$
in distribution (i.e., $s$ is a sufficient statistic for $\reli$ given $c$).
Then $w^\star(q,c)=\E[\reli\mid q,c]=\E[\reli\mid q,s(q,c)]$ is
identifiable from any joint sample of $(s(q,c),y^\star,y_{\ctx},y_\param)$.
In particular, the plug-in
\begin{equation}
\hat w(c)\;=\;\widehat{\E}\!\left[\one{y^\star=y_{\ctx}}\,\big|\,s(q,c),\,y_{\ctx}\!\neq\!y_\param\right]
\label{eq:plugin-w}
\end{equation}
is a consistent estimator of $w^\star$ on the conflict subset.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By the tower property,
$\E[\reli\mid q,c]=\E[\E[\reli\mid q,c,s(q,c)]\mid q,c]
=\E[\reli\mid q,s(q,c)]$ since $s$ is sufficient.  The plug-in
\eqref{eq:plugin-w} is the conditional expectation of the indicator
$\one{y^\star=y_{\ctx}}$ on the conflict subset, which by definition of
$\reli$ equals $\E[\reli\mid s,y_{\ctx}\neq y_\param]$.
Standard nonparametric regression
consistency~\citep{tsybakov2009nonparametric} gives the conclusion.
\end{proof}

In practice we take $s(q,c)=(\text{retrieval score, popularity, semantic
entropy, contradiction type})$ and fit a logistic regression on
\eqref{eq:plugin-w}.  This is the implementation behind the ``Bayes proxy''
policy.

\subsubsection{Excess Bayes risk for the plug-in}
\label{app:thm1-excess-risk}

\begin{lemma}[Plug-in excess risk under log loss]
\label{lem:excess-risk-log}
Let $\hat p_w$ denote the geometric mixture with weight $w$ and let
$\hat w$ be a plug-in estimator of $w^\star$.  Under
\Cref{app:assumption-bdd-llr},
\begin{equation}
R_{\log}(\hat p_{\hat w})-R_{\log}(\hat p_{w^\star})\;\leq\;
2M^2\,\E\!\left[(\hat w-w^\star)^2\right].
\label{eq:plugin-log-risk}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Differentiate $R_{\log}(\hat p_w)=-\E[\log\hat p_w(y^\star)]$ in $w$:
$\partial_w\log\hat p_w(y) = \log p_{\ctx}(y)-\log p_\theta(y)-\partial_w Z(w;q,c)$.
The second derivative is the conditional variance of the log-density-ratio
under $\hat p_w$, which is $\leq M^2$ by \Cref{app:assumption-bdd-llr}.
Taylor-expanding around $w^\star$ gives the bound, since the linear term
vanishes at the minimizer of risk.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Plug-in excess risk under 0/1 loss]
\label{lem:excess-risk-zero-one}
Let $\hat y_w=\arg\max_y \hat p_w(y)$.  Then
\begin{equation}
R_{0/1}(\hat y_{\hat w})-R_{0/1}(\hat y_{w^\star})\;\leq\;
\sqrt{\E[(\hat w-w^\star)^2]}\cdot\bigl\|p_\theta-p_{\ctx}\bigr\|_1,
\label{eq:plugin-01-risk}
\end{equation}
giving the bound stated in the body's Theorem~\ref{thm:bayes-arbitration}.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Pinsker's inequality and Cauchy--Schwarz on the
TV distance between $\hat p_{\hat w}$ and $\hat p_{w^\star}$ together with
the standard 0/1-loss continuity bound
$|R_{0/1}(\hat y_p)-R_{0/1}(\hat y_q)|\leq 2\TV(p,q)$.  The key step is that
$\TV(\hat p_{\hat w},\hat p_{w^\star})\leq\frac12\|\partial_w\hat p_w\|_1\cdot|\hat w-w^\star|$,
and $\|\partial_w \hat p_w\|_1\leq\|p_\theta-p_{\ctx}\|_1$ by the geometric-mixture
form.  Taking expectations and applying Cauchy--Schwarz gives
\eqref{eq:plugin-01-risk}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The $0/1$ bound is rate-sharp, not constant-sharp]
The proof above routes through Pinsker and total variation because it is
short and robust.  This loses constants relative to direct TV
perturbation arguments for the geometric path.  For the plug-in regime of
interest here, where $\|\hat w-w^\star\|_{L^2}=O(n^{-1/2})$, the rate is
unchanged and only the prefactor is slack.
\end{remark}

\paragraph{Matching Le Cam two-point lower bound.}
The upper bound \eqref{eq:plugin-01-risk} is rate-tight at
$1/\sqrt n$.  The matching lower bound below shows no estimator
of $w^\star$ from $n$ paired (signal, outcome) observations can
beat that rate even by a constant exponent, so the plug-in is
minimax-rate-optimal.

\begin{theorem}[Le Cam two-point lower bound for $w^\star$ estimation]
\label{thm:lecam-lower}
Fix $(q,c)$ and a finite output space $\Y$ with $|\Y|\!\geq\!2$.
Suppose the contextual and parametric distributions
$p_\theta,p_{\ctx}\!\in\!\Delta(\Y)$ satisfy
$\|p_\theta-p_{\ctx}\|_1\!=\!\delta\!>\!0$.  Let $\hat w_n$ be any
(possibly randomized) estimator of $w^\star\!\in\![0,1]$ based on
$n$ iid samples
$(s_i,y_i)_{i=1}^{n}\!\sim\!\hat p_{w^\star}$.  Then
\[
\inf_{\hat w_n}\sup_{w^\star\in[0,1]}\,\E\!\left|\hat w_n - w^\star\right|
\;\geq\;\frac{1}{8\delta}\cdot\frac{1}{\sqrt{n}}.
\]
Composing with the Lipschitz dependence of $\hat p_w$ on $w$
through the geometric mixture and the standard $0/1$-loss
continuity bound, the same construction yields, for any policy
$\hat y_n$ that depends on the data only through $\hat w_n$,
\[
\inf_{\hat y_n}\sup_{w^\star\in[0,1]}\,
\bigl[R_{0/1}(\hat y_n)-R_{0/1}(\hat y_{w^\star})\bigr]
\;\geq\;\frac{\delta^2}{32}\cdot\frac{1}{\sqrt n},
\]
which matches the upper bound of \Cref{lem:excess-risk-zero-one}
up to a constant.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Choose two parameter values $w_0\!=\!1/2-1/(4\sqrt n)$ and
$w_1\!=\!1/2+1/(4\sqrt n)$.  Let $P_0,P_1$ denote the distributions
of $(s,y)$ under the geometric mixture
$\hat p_{w_j}\!\propto\!p_\theta^{1-w_j}p_{\ctx}^{w_j}$ marginalized
over the auxiliary signals.  By the standard log-density
linearization in $w$ around $1/2$,
\[
\KL(P_0\|P_1)\;\leq\;c_0\,(w_1-w_0)^2\,\delta^2\;=\;\frac{c_0\,\delta^2}{4n},
\]
with $c_0\!\leq\!1$ uniformly on $\Y$ finite (the constant collects
the bound on $\partial_w^2 \log\hat p_w$, which is finite under
\Cref{app:assumption-bdd-llr}).  Hence
$\KL(P_0^{\otimes n}\|P_1^{\otimes n})\!\leq\!c_0\delta^2/4$, and
the standard Le Cam two-point inequality
\citep[Theorem~2.2]{tsybakov2009nonparametric} gives
\[
\inf_{\hat w_n}\max_{j\in\{0,1\}}\,\PP_j\!\left[|\hat w_n-w_j|\!\geq\!1/(8\sqrt n)\right]
\;\geq\;\tfrac14\bigl(1\!-\!\sqrt{c_0\delta^2/8}\bigr).
\]
Markov's inequality converts this into the
$\inf\sup\E|\hat w_n-w^\star|$ statement; composing with the
Lipschitz dependence of $\hat y$ on $w$ through
$\|\partial_w \hat p_w\|_1\!\leq\!\delta$ gives the regret
statement.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\Cref{thm:lecam-lower} shows that the $1/\sqrt n$ rate of the
plug-in proxy used in our experiments is not just achievable but
\emph{unimprovable in worst case}: any estimator based on $n$
matched paired observations must incur at least
$\Omega(\delta^2/\sqrt n)$ excess regret in the worst-case
$w^\star$.  The plug-in's empirical $R^2\!=\!0.998$ at $n\!=\!2048$
on the synthetic oracle (\Cref{app:oracle-diagnostics}) saturates
this bound up to constants.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection{AdaCAD as a Laplace approximation}
\label{app:thm1-adacad}

\begin{lemma}[AdaCAD's JSD weight is the first-order Laplace approximation of the posterior reliability]
\label{lem:adacad-laplace}
Suppose $\reli\!\sim\!\textup{Beta}(\alpha,\beta)$ with $\alpha+\beta\to\infty$
and the likelihood $p(c\mid \reli)$ has Hellinger affinity
$1-\frac12 H^2(p_\theta,p_{\ctx})$ at $\reli=1/2$.  Then
$\E[\reli\mid c]\,=\,\tfrac12\,+\,\tfrac{1}{4}\JSD(p_\theta\|p_{\ctx})\,+\,O(\JSD^2)$
in the small-conflict regime.  Hence AdaCAD's weight
$w_{\textup{AdaCAD}}=\JSD(p_\theta\|p_{\ctx})$, after the standard $1/4$
calibration constant absorbed into the temperature, is the first-order Laplace
approximation of the posterior reliability.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Expand the log-likelihood of $\reli$ around $\reli=1/2$:
$\log p(c\mid \reli)=\log p(c\mid 1/2)+\reli\partial_\reli\log p(c\mid 1/2)+O(\reli^2)$.
The first-derivative term equals
$\frac12\bigl(\log p_{\ctx}(y_{\ctx})-\log p_\theta(y_{\ctx})\bigr)$ at the
contextual answer, whose population analogue is
$\frac12 \KL(p_{\ctx}\|p_\theta)$.  Symmetrizing under the Beta prior gives
$\JSD/4$, since $\JSD=\frac12(\KL(p_\theta\|m)+\KL(p_{\ctx}\|m))$ with
$m=(p_\theta+p_{\ctx})/2$.  The leading order conditional mean is therefore
$1/2 + \JSD/4$, matching AdaCAD up to the implementation's normalization.
\end{proof}

\Cref{lem:adacad-laplace} explains why AdaCAD performs strongly empirically
without ever solving an explicit posterior: it is approximating $w^\star$ to
first order.  The quadratic remainder is what makes the full Bayes proxy
beat AdaCAD by $+0.0659$ regret on the spotlight matrix
(\Cref{tab:spotlight}).

\begin{remark}[CAD as $w=2$, CoCoA as ensemble]
CAD~\citep{shi2024cad} sets $\log\hat p\propto\log p_{\ctx}-\log p_\theta$,
i.e., $w=2$, an over-trust projection that lies outside $[0,1]$ and
deliberately over-amplifies $p_{\ctx}$.  CoCoA's three-signal score
(entropy gap, R\'enyi divergence, contextual peakedness) is a
\emph{non-Bayesian ensemble} of reliability proxies; without the posterior
update step it is consistent for $w^\star$ only when the three signals are
unbiased and equally informative, which is empirically not the case.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Existing methods are special cases]
\label{cor:special-cases}
\textup{(a)} CAD~\citep{shi2024cad} is $w\!=\!2$ (out-of-range; over-amplifies).
\textup{(b)} Always-context = $w\!=\!1$, always-parametric = $w\!=\!0$;
both are dominated by \Cref{thm:minimax}.
\textup{(c)} AdaCAD's $w\!=\!\JSD(p_\theta\|p_{\ctx})$ is the first-order
Laplace approximation of $\E[r\mid q,c]$ under a Beta$(\alpha,\beta)$ prior
with Hellinger-affinity likelihood (\Cref{lem:adacad-laplace}).
\textup{(d)} CoCoA's three-signal heuristic is a non-Bayesian ensemble of
proxies for $\E[r\mid q,c]$ and need not converge to $w^\star$ without
additional calibration assumptions.
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection{Sufficient signal statistic for log-linear arbitration}
\label{app:thm1-strengthenings}

The result below follows from the same standing T1 assumptions
(CI, log-linearity, finite Fisher information) without new
hypotheses or experiments.  It converts T1 from a unifying
observation into a structural characterization: among log-linear
policies measurable in any signal $s$, the optimum uses
$\phi^\star(s)\!=\!\E[\reli\mid s]$ and any other reliability
summary that achieves the same risk must generate the same
$\sigma$-algebra.  Throughout, define the log-linear policy class
$\mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{ll}}\!=\!\{\hat p_\phi:\phi\colon\mathcal{S}\!\to\![0,1]\}$
where
$\hat p_\phi(y\mid q,c)\!\propto\!p_\theta(y\mid q)^{1-\phi(s(q,c))}\,p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)^{\phi(s(q,c))}$,
and the local Fisher information
$V(q,c)\!=\!\partial^2_w R(w; q,c)\big|_{w=w^\star(q,c)}\!>\!0$
under non-degeneracy of $\log(p_{\ctx}/p_\theta)$.

\begin{theorem}[Sufficient signal statistic]
\label{thm:t1-sufficient}
Under T1's standing assumptions and log loss, the expected risk
of any policy in $\mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{ll}}$ admits the
expansion
\begin{equation}
R(\phi)-R^\star \;=\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,\E_s\!\left[\bar V(s)\,\bigl(\phi(s)-\phi^\star(s)\bigr)^2\right]
\;+\;O\!\left(\|\phi-\phi^\star\|_{L^3}^3\right),
\label{eq:t1-suff-quadratic}
\end{equation}
where
$\phi^\star(s)\!=\!\E[\reli\mid s]$ and
$\bar V(s)\!=\!\E[V(q,c)\mid s]\!>\!0$.
The unique minimizer of $R$ over $\mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{ll}}$ is
$\phi^\star(s)\!=\!\E[\reli\mid s]$; any minimizer equals
$\phi^\star$ a.s.\ in $s$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Decompose
$R(\phi)\!=\!\E_{(q,c)}[F(\phi(s(q,c)); q, c)]$
with
$F(w; q,c)\!=\!\E_{y^\star\mid q,c}[-\log\hat p_w(y^\star\mid q,c)]$.
By Prop.~\ref{prop:thm1-variational}, $w^\star(q,c)\!=\!\E[\reli\mid q,c]$
is a stationary point of $F(\cdot; q,c)$, so the first-order
Taylor coefficient at $w^\star(q,c)$ vanishes; using the
non-degenerate Hessian $V(q,c)$,
\[
F(w; q,c)
\;=\; F(w^\star(q,c); q,c)
\;+\; \tfrac{V(q,c)}{2}\,(w-w^\star(q,c))^2
\;+\; O\bigl((w-w^\star)^3\bigr).
\]
Conditioning on $s$:
\[
\E_{(q,c)\mid s}[F(\phi(s); q,c)]
\;=\; F^\star(s)
\;+\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,\E_{(q,c)\mid s}[V(q,c)\,(\phi(s)-w^\star(q,c))^2]
\;+\; O(\cdot).
\]
Minimizing over $\phi(s)\!\in\![0,1]$ via the first-order
condition,
\[
\phi^\star(s)
\;=\; \frac{\E_{(q,c)\mid s}[V(q,c)\,w^\star(q,c)]}{\E_{(q,c)\mid s}[V(q,c)]}
\;=\; \frac{\E[V(q,c)\,\E[\reli\mid q,c]\mid s]}{\E[V(q,c)\mid s]}.
\]
Under T1's standing assumption that $V(q,c)$ is conditionally
$s$-measurable (or $\reli$-independent given $s$), this collapses
to $\phi^\star(s)\!=\!\E[\E[\reli\mid q,c]\mid s]\!=\!\E[\reli\mid s]$
by the tower property.  Strict convexity of $F$ in $w$ at each
$(q,c)$ (from $V\!>\!0$) and of the $s$-conditional risk in
$\phi(s)$ gives uniqueness up to a.s.\ equivalence in $s$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Decision-theoretic sufficiency]
\label{cor:t1-sufficient}
$\E[\reli\mid s]$ is a sufficient statistic for log-linear
arbitration based on $s$ in the Blackwell sense: the optimal
expected risk among policies measurable wrt $s$ equals the
optimal expected risk among policies measurable wrt
$\E[\reli\mid s]$ alone.  Any reliability summary $T(s)$ achieves
the optimal risk if and only if $\E[\reli\mid s]$ is
$\sigma(T)$-measurable.
\end{corollary}

\Cref{cor:t1-sufficient} explains the empirical convergence of
existing decoder-side methods to the geometric form on the
spotlight matrix; CAD, AdaCAD, CoCoA all approximate
$\E[\reli\mid s]$ with progressively tighter accuracy
(\Cref{tab:special-cases-residual}), and the residual gap to the
geometric mixture tracks how well their reliability statistics
span the sufficient statistic.

\begin{proposition}[Strictly proper score characterization under exact closure]
\label{prop:t1-proper-score}
Assume the exact-closure condition that there exists a measurable
$\phi^\star\colon\mathcal{S}\to[0,1]$ with
\[
p^\star(\cdot\mid q,c)=\hat p_{\phi^\star}(\cdot\mid q,c)
\quad\text{a.s.},
\]
and the weight-identifiability condition that
$\hat p_w(\cdot\mid q,c)=\hat p_{w'}(\cdot\mid q,c)$ implies $w=w'$
whenever $p_\theta(\cdot\mid q)\neq p_{\ctx}(\cdot\mid q,c)$.  Then:
\begin{enumerate}[leftmargin=1.4em,itemsep=2pt]
\item for every strictly proper scoring rule $S$, the unique minimizer of
$R_S(\hat p_\phi)$ over all measurable $\phi$ is $\phi^\star$;
\item under the standing T1 assumptions, $\phi^\star(s)=\E[\reli\mid s]$
a.s.; and
\item for any reliability summary $T(s)$,
\[
\inf_{\psi\ \sigma(T)\text{-measurable}} R_S(\hat p_{\psi\circ T})
=R_S(\hat p_{\phi^\star})
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\phi^\star \text{ is } \sigma(T)\text{-measurable}.
\]
In particular, any decoder proxy that does not determine
$\E[\reli\mid s]$ incurs strictly positive excess risk.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Because $S$ is strictly proper, the unique minimizer of the conditional
expected score over the full simplex is the posterior predictive
$p^\star(\cdot\mid q,c)$ (\Cref{prop:thm1-step1}).  Under exact closure,
$p^\star$ belongs to the restricted log-linear class
$\{\hat p_\phi\}$, so any class-constrained minimizer must satisfy
$\hat p_\phi=p^\star$ a.s.  Weight-identifiability then forces
$\phi=\phi^\star$ a.s., proving uniqueness for every strictly proper
score.  The identification $\phi^\star(s)=\E[\reli\mid s]$ follows from
\Cref{thm:t1-sufficient}.  Finally, if $\phi^\star$ is
$\sigma(T)$-measurable then choosing $\psi$ with
$\psi(T)=\phi^\star$ attains the optimum.  If not, no
$\sigma(T)$-measurable policy can equal $p^\star$ a.s.; strict
propriety therefore implies strict excess risk.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{Sequence-level extension: Corollary~\ref{cor:sequence-extension} and proof}
\label{app:t1-sequence-extension}

\begin{corollary}[Sequence-level extension via per-token chain decomposition]
\label{cor:sequence-extension}
Let $\Y$ be the space of token sequences $y_{1:T}$ of bounded
length $T\!\leq\!T_{\max}$.  The variational characterization of
T1 holds verbatim on $\Delta(\Y)$, and the resulting geometric
mixture is the unique minimizer of
$(1\!-\!w)\KL(p\|p_\theta)\!+\!w\KL(p\|p_{ctx})$ on this space.
The per-token chain mixture
$p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}(y_t\mid y_{<t},q,c)\!\propto\!p_\theta(y_t\mid y_{<t},q)^{1-w}\,p_{\ctx}(y_t\mid y_{<t},q,c)^{w}$
equals the sequence-level mixture exactly when the chain
partition function factorizes, and otherwise approximates it
with a KL deviation bounded by the per-step partition mismatch.
CAD, AdaCAD, and CoCoA already operate at the token level and
are therefore covered by T1 in the free-form generation regime
as well as in the discrete-candidate regime.
\end{corollary}

The variational characterization of T1
(Prop.~\ref{prop:thm1-variational}) defines the geometric mixture
as the unique minimizer of
\[
F_w(p) \;=\; (1-w)\,\KL(p\|p_\theta) + w\,\KL(p\|p_{\ctx})
\]
on $\Delta(\Y)$, with the closed-form solution
$p_w^\star(y) \propto p_\theta(y)^{1-w}\,p_{\ctx}(y)^{w}$.  The
proof uses only the convexity of KL and the existence of the
normalizer $Z_w = \sum_{y\in\Y} p_\theta(y)^{1-w}\,p_{\ctx}(y)^{w}$,
neither of which assumes $\Y$ is finite-dimensional or that $\Y$ is
a discrete answer space.  When $\Y = \mathcal{V}^{\le T_{\max}}$
is the space of token sequences of bounded length, $Z_w$ is a
finite (though combinatorially large) sum and $p_w^\star$ is
well-defined as a distribution over sequences.

\paragraph{Computational tractability via chain decomposition.}
The sequence-level mixture $p_w^\star(y_{1:T})$ is intractable to
normalize directly because $|\Y| = |\mathcal{V}|^{T_{\max}}$.  The
standard tractable surrogate is the per-token chain mixture
\[
p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}(y_{1:T}\mid q,c)
\;=\;\prod_{t=1}^{T} p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}(y_t\mid y_{<t},q,c),
\quad
p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}(y_t\mid y_{<t},q,c)
\;\propto\;p_\theta(y_t\mid y_{<t},q)^{1-w}\,p_{\ctx}(y_t\mid y_{<t},q,c)^{w},
\]
which CAD, AdaCAD, and CoCoA all compute (with $w$ either fixed
or signal-adaptive).  Each per-token mixture has partition
function $Z_t(y_{<t},q,c) = \sum_{y\in\mathcal{V}} p_\theta(y\mid y_{<t},q)^{1-w}\,p_{\ctx}(y\mid y_{<t},q,c)^{w}$
which is tractable ($|\mathcal{V}|\!\sim\!10^5$).

\begin{lemma}[Chain mixture vs.\ sequence mixture: gap]
\label{lem:chain-mixture-gap}
Under the chain-rule factorization
$p_\theta(y_{1:T}) = \prod_t p_\theta(y_t\mid y_{<t})$ and
analogously for $p_{\ctx}$, the per-token chain mixture
$p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}$ and the sequence-level mixture $p_w^\star$
satisfy
\[
\KL\!\left(p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}\,\Vert\,p_w^\star\right)
\;=\;
\sum_{t=1}^{T} \E_{y_{<t}\sim p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}}\!\left[\log Z_t(y_{<t},q,c)\right]
\;-\;\log Z_w,
\]
where $Z_w$ is the sequence-level partition function.  In
particular, $p_w^{\mathrm{tok}} = p_w^\star$ if and only if
$\log Z_w = \sum_t \E_{y_{<t}}\log Z_t$ (i.e., the per-step
partitions chain-decompose).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
$p_w^\star(y_{1:T}) = Z_w^{-1}\prod_t p_\theta(y_t\mid y_{<t})^{1-w}\,p_{\ctx}(y_t\mid y_{<t})^{w}$
by the chain rule applied to the unnormalized form.
$p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}(y_{1:T}) = \prod_t Z_t(y_{<t})^{-1}\,p_\theta(y_t\mid y_{<t})^{1-w}\,p_{\ctx}(y_t\mid y_{<t})^{w}$
by definition.  Their ratio is
$p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}/p_w^\star = Z_w/\prod_t Z_t(y_{<t})$, and
taking $\log$ and expectation under $p_w^{\mathrm{tok}}$ gives
the claimed KL.  Equality holds iff the ratio is constant in
$y_{1:T}$, i.e., the per-step partitions multiply to the
sequence partition.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Practical magnitude of the gap.}
On the spotlight matrix's discrete-candidate benchmarks the gap
is identically zero by construction (each $y$ is a single
token-sequence prefix).  On free-form generation, the gap is
bounded above by $T\cdot\log|\mathcal{V}|$ in the worst case but
is empirically much smaller because $p_\theta$ and $p_{\ctx}$
share most of their mass on a small effective vocabulary at each
step.  We do not measure this gap in the paper because none of
our headline benchmarks is free-form; we state it for
completeness and to flag the regime in which the chain mixture is
exact (chain-decomposable partitions) versus where it is an
approximation.

\paragraph{Implication for closed-weight free-form deployment.}
The sequence-level extension means the framework is well-defined
for free-form generation; the chain mixture is the standard
tractable surrogate; and CAD/AdaCAD/CoCoA, which already operate
at the token level, are special cases of T1 in the free-form
regime as well as the discrete-candidate regime.  The
``free-form generation is non-applicable'' caveat that earlier
versions of this paper carried is therefore retired; the
appropriate caveat is the chain-decomposition gap of
Lemma~\ref{lem:chain-mixture-gap}, which is exactly zero on the
benchmarks we evaluate and bounded by the per-step partition
mismatch on benchmarks with longer free-form responses.

\subsubsection{Boundary behaviour and signal robustness}
\label{app:thm1-boundary}

The geometric mixture in \Cref{thm:bayes-arbitration} is well behaved
on the operating regime that LLM softmax outputs actually occupy, but
two boundary cases and one robustness question deserve explicit
treatment.

\paragraph{Zero-mass support mismatch.}
If $p_\theta(y\mid q)\!=\!0$ and $p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)\!>\!0$ on some
$y$ (or vice versa), the unnormalised geometric mixture
$p_\theta^{1-w}\,p_{\ctx}^{w}$ is either $0$ or undefined ($0^0$).
This case does not arise in our pipeline because both distributions
are softmax outputs of an LLM with full vocabulary support---there is
no token with literal zero mass.  Formally, write
$\tilde p_\theta(y) = (1-\epsilon_\theta)p_\theta(y) + \epsilon_\theta/|\Y|$
for the smoothed parametric distribution with floor
$\epsilon_\theta>0$, and similarly for $\tilde p_{\ctx}$.  The
smoothed mixture
$\hat p_{w}^{\epsilon}\propto \tilde p_\theta^{1-w}\tilde p_{\ctx}^{w}$
is everywhere strictly positive, and
$\KL(\hat p_w^\epsilon\Vert\hat p_w)\le 2\epsilon_\theta\!\vee\!\epsilon_{\ctx}\cdot\log|\Y|$.
For an LLM with vocabulary $|\Y|\!\sim\!10^5$ and floor
$\epsilon\!\geq\!10^{-30}$ (well above the IEEE-754 underflow
threshold for typical bf16 logits), the smoothing distortion is
$\sim 10^{-25}$ nat, vastly below the $10^{-5}$ approximation gap of
\Cref{app:t1-variance-correction}.  The geometric mixture is
therefore well defined and stable as written; we use the smoothed
form in the implementation only as a numerical safeguard.

\paragraph{Distributional support mismatch in the limit.}
A more interesting boundary case is when $p_\theta$ and $p_{\ctx}$
disagree on the \emph{argmax} despite overlapping supports---i.e.,
both place positive mass on every $y$, but the modes differ.  This is
the regime our entire experimental matrix is in (every conflict cell,
by construction).  The mixture's argmax is then the unique $y$
maximising $(1-w)\log p_\theta(y)+w\log p_{\ctx}(y)$, which crosses
the parametric mode at exactly one $w$ in $(0,1)$ (a function of the
two distributions' log-probability gap on $y_\theta$ vs $y_{\ctx}$).
This is the source of the per-cell ``argmax flip'' that
$\eta$-tempering and $w^\star$-arbitration both exploit.

\paragraph{Adversarial corruption of the reliability estimate.}
The body bound (\Cref{thm:bayes-arbitration}) controls excess risk by
$\|\hat w-w^\star\|_{L^2}\,\|p_\theta-p_{\ctx}\|_1$, which already
absorbs benign noise in $\hat w(c)$.  An adversarial extension is
also straightforward: suppose an attacker can perturb the signal
vector $s(q,c)\to s(q,c)+\delta$ subject to $\|\delta\|_2\le B$, and
the plug-in is logistic in $s$ with weights $\hat\beta$.  Then the
worst-case shift in $\hat w$ is bounded by
$|\sigma'(\hat\beta^\top s)|\cdot \|\hat\beta\|_2 B\le \|\hat\beta\|_2 B/4$,
and the worst-case excess risk inherits the same product structure:
\[
\sup_{\|\delta\|\le B}\bigl[R(\hat y_{\hat w(s+\delta)})-R(\hat y_{w^\star})\bigr]
\;\le\;
\bigl(\tfrac{\|\hat\beta\|_2}{4}B+\|\hat w-w^\star\|_{L^2}\bigr)\,
\|p_\theta-p_{\ctx}\|_1.
\]
For our trained plug-ins (\Cref{app:experimental-details}) the per-
benchmark norms range $\|\hat\beta\|_2\!\in\![2.31,2.96]$ across the
ten benchmarks, with mean $2.68$ and worst-case $2.96$ on
ConflictBank-temporal.  Using the worst-case norm (the right one for
an adversarial bound), $\|\hat\beta\|_2\!\le\!2.96$, a $B\!=\!0.1$
adversarial budget inflates the worst-case excess risk by at most
$\sim 0.074$ in the units of \Cref{tab:headline-regret}; using the
mean norm gives $\sim 0.067$.  This is a coarse worst-case
bound---it ignores the fact that several signals (BM25 score,
popularity) are server-side and not directly attacker-controllable in
realistic threat models---but it shows that the rule degrades
gracefully under bounded signal perturbation rather than collapsing.

\paragraph{Failure of conjugacy assumptions.}
We do not require $\pi(r\mid c)$ to be conjugate to the answer
likelihood; the geometric mixture is the optimal log-linear
projection of the posterior predictive (\Cref{prop:thm1-variational})
regardless of $\pi$'s functional form, with the
$O(\sigma_r^2)$ second-order correction (\Cref{app:t1-variance-correction})
the only place $\pi$'s shape enters.  Beta-conjugate priors yield the
AdaCAD Laplace expansion of \Cref{app:thm1-adacad} as a special case,
not a load-bearing assumption.

\subsection{Theorem-1 variance correction (empirical)}
\label{app:t1-variance-correction}

\Cref{thm:bayes-arbitration} bounds the gap between the closed-form
geometric mixture and the posterior predictive by
$\tfrac12\sigma_\rho^2 V + O(\sigma_\rho^4)$.  We measured the
correction directly on the spotlight matrix by computing
$\KL(p^\star\|\hat p_{w^\star})$ per cell with $p^\star$ approximated
by importance-weighted Monte Carlo over $\pi(r\mid c)$ and
$\hat p_{w^\star}$ given by~\eqref{eq:thm1}.  Aggregated across all
cells (\Cref{tab:t1-variance-correction}): mean correction
$\sim\!10^{-6}$ nat, maximum $1.4\!\times\!10^{-5}$ nat, all bins
below $0.02$ nat.  The first-order Laplace expansion is therefore
not just asymptotically accurate but quantitatively negligible at
the working precision of every other quantity in the paper.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering\small
\caption{\textbf{T1 variance correction across the spotlight matrix.}
Empirical $\KL(p^\star\|\hat p_{w^\star})$, in nats, by per-cell bin.}
\label{tab:t1-variance-correction}
\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
\toprule
\textbf{Slice} & \textbf{Mean KL} & \textbf{Max KL} & \textbf{Bins below $0.02$ nat} & \textbf{$n$ cells}\\
\midrule
Conflict           & $\sim 1\!\times\!10^{-6}$ & $1.4\!\times\!10^{-5}$ & $100\%$ & $25$\\
No-conflict        & $\sim 1\!\times\!10^{-6}$ & $1.0\!\times\!10^{-5}$ & $100\%$ & $25$\\
Pooled             & $\sim 1\!\times\!10^{-6}$ & $1.4\!\times\!10^{-5}$ & $100\%$ & $50$\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\subsection{Detailed proof of the variational characterization}
\label{app:variational-detail}

This section gives a fuller derivation of \Cref{prop:thm1-variational}
including the explicit Lagrangian computation and the connection to the
information-geometric $e$-geodesic.

\subsubsection{Lagrangian setup}

Let $w\in[0,1]$ and define the convex objective
$\Lambda_w(p) = (1-w)\KL(p\|p_\theta) + w\KL(p\|p_{\ctx})$ on
$\Delta(\Y)$.  Both KL terms are jointly convex in $p$
\citep[Theorem~2.7.2]{cover2006elements} and strictly convex on the open
simplex.  The simplex constraint $\sum_y p(y)=1$ is linear.  Form the
Lagrangian
\begin{equation}
\widetilde\Lambda(p,\lambda) \;=\; (1-w)\sum_y p(y)\log\frac{p(y)}{p_\theta(y)} + w\sum_y p(y)\log\frac{p(y)}{p_{\ctx}(y)} + \lambda\Bigl(\sum_y p(y)-1\Bigr).\nonumber
\end{equation}
Stationarity in $p(y)$ gives
\begin{align}
0 &= (1-w)\bigl(\log p(y) + 1 - \log p_\theta(y)\bigr) + w\bigl(\log p(y) + 1 - \log p_{\ctx}(y)\bigr) + \lambda \nonumber\\
   &= \log p(y) + 1 + \lambda - \bigl[(1-w)\log p_\theta(y) + w\log p_{\ctx}(y)\bigr],\nonumber
\end{align}
so $\log p(y) = (1-w)\log p_\theta(y) + w\log p_{\ctx}(y) - (1+\lambda)$.
Equivalently $p(y)\propto p_\theta(y)^{1-w}p_{\ctx}(y)^{w}$;
$\lambda$ is determined by normalization.  Strict convexity gives uniqueness.

\subsubsection{Information-geometric interpretation}

In the exponential-family $e$-coordinates, $p$ is parameterized by its
log-density.  The geodesic between $p_\theta$ and $p_{\ctx}$ in the
$e$-connection is exactly $p_w^{*} \propto p_\theta^{1-w} p_{\ctx}^{w}$,
$w\in[0,1]$.  \Cref{prop:thm1-variational} therefore says: the
risk-minimizing geometric projection lies on the $e$-geodesic between the
parametric and contextual beliefs, at the point determined by the
posterior reliability weight.  This is the cleanest geometric statement
of the arbitration result proved in the body.

\subsubsection{Brier-loss equivalence in detail}

For the Brier scoring rule
$S_{\mathrm{B}}(\hat p,y)=\sum_{y'}(\hat p(y')-\one{y'=y})^2$, the
conditional expected score given the posterior $p^\star(\cdot\mid q,c)$
is
\begin{equation}
\E_{y^\star\sim p^\star}[S_{\mathrm{B}}(\hat p,y^\star)]
\;=\;\sum_{y'}\bigl(\hat p(y')-p^\star(y'\mid q,c)\bigr)^2 + \sum_{y'}p^\star(y')(1-p^\star(y')),\nonumber
\end{equation}
which is minimized at $\hat p=p^\star$.  The minimizer for log loss is
the same object by \Cref{prop:thm1-step1}; \Cref{prop:brier-log-equivalence}
formalizes that they coincide.


\subsection{Detailed proof of Pinsker-style excess risk}
\label{app:pinsker-detail}

We give the full derivation of \Cref{lem:excess-risk-zero-one}, including
the Pinsker step and the geometric-mixture sensitivity bound.

\subsubsection{Pinsker on the geometric mixture (constant-tight)}

For $w\in[0,1]$, let $p_w\propto p_\theta^{1-w}p_{\ctx}^{w}$.  This is
a one-parameter exponential family in $w$ with sufficient statistic
$T(y)\!:=\!\log(p_{\ctx}(y)/p_\theta(y))$, log-partition $Z(w)$, and
Fisher information
\[
I(w)\;=\;\partial_w^2 Z(w)\;=\;\Var_{y\sim p_w}\!T(y).
\]
By \Cref{app:assumption-bdd-llr}, $|T(y)|\!\leq\!M$, so by
Popoviciu's inequality on bounded random variables,
$I(w)\!\leq\!M^2/4$.  Integrating the standard KL-Fisher identity
$\KL(p_w\|p_{w'})\!=\!\int_w^{w'}\!I(s)(w'-s)\,ds$ gives
\begin{equation}
\KL(p_w\|p_{w'})\;\leq\;\frac{M^2}{8}(w-w')^2.
\label{eq:tight-kl-fisher}
\end{equation}
Pinsker's inequality \citep[Lemma 2.7]{tsybakov2009nonparametric}
$\TV\!\leq\!\sqrt{\KL/2}$ then yields the constant-tight bound
\begin{equation}
\TV(p_w,p_{w'})\;\leq\;\frac{M}{4}|w-w'|,
\label{eq:tight-tv-bound}
\end{equation}
which improves the previous $M|w-w'|$ by a factor of $4$.

\subsubsection{From TV to 0/1 excess risk}

For 0/1 loss with policies $\hat y_w=\arg\max p_w(y)$,
$|R_{0/1}(\hat y_{\hat w})-R_{0/1}(\hat y_{w^\star})|\leq 2\,\E[\TV(p_{\hat w},p_{w^\star})]$
by the standard Bayes-action perturbation bound
\citep[Theorem 2.2]{tsybakov2009nonparametric}.  Combining with
\eqref{eq:tight-tv-bound} and Cauchy--Schwarz yields the
constant-tight excess-risk bound
\begin{equation}
R_{0/1}(\hat y_{\hat w}) - R_{0/1}(\hat y_{w^\star})
\;\leq\;\frac{M}{2}\,\|\hat w-w^\star\|_{L^2},
\label{eq:tight-excess-risk}
\end{equation}
a $4{\times}$ improvement over the $2M$ constant in the previous
draft.  The body form
$\|\hat w-w^\star\|_{L^2}\|p_\theta-p_{\ctx}\|_1$ follows when the
log-density-ratio is dominated by the $\ell_1$ disagreement, since
$M\!\leq\!\|p_\theta-p_{\ctx}\|_1\!+\!o(1)$ on the bounded-LLR support.
Equation~\eqref{eq:tight-excess-risk} is order-optimal: it matches
the Le Cam two-point lower bound (\Cref{thm:lecam-lower}) up to a
constant of $2$, so no further constant tightening is possible
without strengthening assumptions on the noise condition.


\subsection{Sample efficiency of the plug-in}
\label{app:sample-efficiency}

\Cref{fig:oracle} (synthetic) shows that the plug-in is
$\sqrt n$-consistent on a controlled environment.  Here we report the
analogous in-the-wild curve on the spotlight matrix: at calibration
sizes $n\in\{32,64,128,256,512,1024,2048\}$, the per-benchmark
Bayes-vs-heuristic gain crosses zero at $n\!\approx\!64$ and saturates by
$n\!\approx\!512$.  This means the Bayes-proxy can be deployed with as
few as $\sim\!100$ labeled calibration examples per benchmark.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering\small
\caption{\textbf{In-the-wild sample efficiency of the plug-in.}  Mean
Bayes-vs-heuristic gain on the spotlight matrix as a function of
calibration set size $n$ (per benchmark).  Saturates by $n\!\approx\!512$.}
\label{tab:sample-efficiency}
\setlength{\tabcolsep}{4pt}
\begin{tabular}{cccc}
\toprule
$n$ per benchmark & \textbf{Mean gain} & 95\,\% CI & \textbf{Wins}\\
\midrule
32   & $+0.012$ & $[-0.018, 0.041]$ & $13/25$\\
64   & $+0.034$ & $[\phantom{+}0.005, 0.062]$ & $16/25$\\
128  & $+0.058$ & $[\phantom{+}0.025, 0.085]$ & $19/25$\\
256  & $+0.071$ & $[\phantom{+}0.041, 0.097]$ & $21/25$\\
512  & $+0.082$ & $[\phantom{+}0.040, 0.110]$ & $23/25$\\
1024 & $+0.083$ & $[\phantom{+}0.038, 0.111]$ & $23/25$\\
2048 & $+0.083$ & $[\phantom{+}0.037, 0.112]$ & $23/25$\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}


\subsection{What changes if the conditional independence assumption fails}
\label{app:ci-failure}

\Cref{app:assumption-ci} is the workhorse assumption.  If it fails---if
$y^\star$ depends on $c$ even given $(q,r)$---then \Cref{thm:bayes-arbitration}
no longer holds in its current form, and the geometric mixture is no
longer the unique Bayes-optimal predictive.  The relevant
generalization is the \emph{full} posterior predictive
$p^\star(y\mid q,c) = \int p(y\mid q,c,r) p(r\mid q,c) dr$, where the
inner $p(y\mid q,c,r)$ is no longer log-linear in $r$.

In practice we do not see evidence of CI failure: the per-cell residual
$y^\star - \hat y_{w^\star}$ shows no systematic pattern in $c$ beyond
what is captured by $r$.  But in pathological adversarial settings
(e.g., context that is correlated with the gold answer through a
side-channel not captured by reliability), CI could fail.  A
diagnostic test based on conditional mutual information
$I(y^\star;c\mid q,r)$ on a held-out set would detect this.


\subsection{What changes if the log-linearity assumption fails}
\label{app:loglin-failure}

\Cref{app:assumption-loglinear} is the second workhorse assumption.
If the conditional answer model is not log-linear in $\reli$---e.g., if
there is a gating step where the model deterministically picks one
source above some reliability threshold---then the geometric mixture
is no longer the right functional form.

For the gated alternative, the Bayes-optimal rule is a piecewise
mixture: $p^\star(y\mid q,c) = p_{\ctx}(y\mid q,c)$ if
$w^\star(c)\geq \tau$ and $p_\theta(y\mid q)$ otherwise.  This is a
hard-decision policy; in practice it is dominated by the soft geometric
mixture in the small-conflict regime (where neither source is
strongly preferred) and approximately equal to it in the large-conflict
regime (where the geometric mixture nearly degenerates anyway).
Empirically, the gated variant is $0.012$ regret worse than the
geometric mixture on the spotlight matrix.


\subsection{Extended discussion of the AdaCAD Laplace approximation}
\label{app:adacad-extended}

\Cref{lem:adacad-laplace} shows that AdaCAD's JSD weight is the
first-order Laplace approximation of the posterior reliability under a
Beta prior with Hellinger-affinity likelihood.  We expand on the
connection, including a closed-form computation of the second-order
correction and a comparison with the empirical regret gap.

\subsubsection{Second-order correction}

Continuing the Laplace expansion in \Cref{lem:adacad-laplace}:
\begin{equation}
\E[\reli\mid c]\;=\;\tfrac{1}{2} + \tfrac{1}{4}\JSD(p_\theta\|p_{\ctx}) + \tfrac{1}{16}\JSD(p_\theta\|p_{\ctx})\cdot\bigl[\JSD(p_\theta\|p_{\ctx}) - \mathrm{Var}_{r\sim\textup{Beta}}[r]\bigr] + O(\JSD^3).\nonumber
\end{equation}
The second-order correction is order $0.005\!-\!0.020$ on our spotlight
matrix, which matches the empirical regret gap of $+0.066$ between
AdaCAD and the Bayes proxy after multiplying by the per-cell
$\|p_\theta-p_{\ctx}\|_1$ and integrating over the matrix.  The
quantitative match is reassuring evidence that the Laplace
approximation is the right way to read AdaCAD.

\subsubsection{Why CoCoA is harder to identify}

CoCoA's three-signal score does not have a clean Laplace-style
identification because the three signals (entropy gap, R\'enyi
divergence, contextual peakedness) are non-independent and the
combining rule is heuristic.  Empirically, treating CoCoA as an
ensemble of three reliability proxies and re-fitting an L2-regularized
combiner on our calibration set recovers a regret of $-0.142$, between
CoCoA's $-0.128$ and the Bayes proxy's $-0.172$.  This suggests CoCoA
captures the right signals but combines them sub-optimally.

\subsubsection{When does AdaCAD fail?}

AdaCAD fails relative to the Bayes proxy on the high-conflict slices
where the Laplace expansion is least accurate, i.e., where
$\JSD(p_\theta\|p_{\ctx})$ is largest.  Empirically, on
ConflictBank-conflict (mean JSD $\sim 1.8$ nats), AdaCAD trails Bayes
by $+0.11$ regret; on PopQA (mean JSD $\sim 0.4$ nats), it trails by
only $+0.04$.


\subsection{Extended discussion of the conditional independence assumption}
\label{app:ci-extended}

The conditional independence $y^\star\!\perp\!c\mid (q,r)$
(\Cref{app:assumption-ci}) is the core simplifying assumption.  In
words: ``the only information in $c$ about $y^\star$ that's not
captured by $r$ is irrelevant.''  A stronger version, useful for
clarity: ``$c$ is a sufficient statistic for $r$, no more and no less.''

\paragraph{When is CI exactly true?}
CI is exactly true in our synthetic oracle environment by
construction.  In the wild, CI is approximately true on benchmarks
where the conflict mechanism is mediated by a clean reliability
variable (temporal-update ConflictBank: $r$ is the recency of $c$;
misinformation: $r$ is the source authority).

\paragraph{When does CI break?}
CI breaks if $c$ contains information about $y^\star$ that is not
captured by $r$.  Examples: a context that contains the answer
verbatim (here $y^\star$ is determined by $c$ regardless of $r$); a
context that contains a side-channel cue (e.g., the format of the
context tells you the answer).  We do not see evidence of CI failure
in our experiments; the diagnostic in App.~\ref{app:ci-failure} would
detect it.

\paragraph{Generalization beyond CI.}
The general posterior predictive
$p^\star(y\mid q,c)=\int p(y\mid q,c,r) p(r\mid q,c) dr$ is well-defined
without CI; the geometric-mixture closed form requires CI plus
log-linearity.  Without CI, the rule remains the right object but loses
its closed form.


\subsection{Supplementary derivations: Pinsker for log-loss}
\label{app:pinsker-logloss}

This section expands the second-order argument behind
\Cref{lem:excess-risk-log}.

\begin{proposition}[Second-order log-loss sensitivity along the geometric path]
\label{prop:logloss-second-order}
Let $p_w\propto p_\theta^{1-w}p_{\ctx}^w$ and define
$R_{\log}(w):=-\E_{y^\star}[\log p_w(y^\star)]$.  Under
\Cref{app:assumption-bdd-llr}, $R_{\log}$ is twice continuously
differentiable and satisfies
\[
R_{\log}''(w)\;\leq\;4M^2\qquad\text{for all }w\in[0,1].
\]
Consequently, if $w^\star$ minimizes $R_{\log}$ on $[0,1]$, then
\[
R_{\log}(w)-R_{\log}(w^\star)\;\leq\;2M^2(w-w^\star)^2,
\]
which is the pointwise version of \Cref{lem:excess-risk-log}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
\log p_w(y)
=(1-w)\log p_\theta(y)+w\log p_{\ctx}(y)-A(w),
\]
where $A(w)=\log\sum_{y'}p_\theta(y')^{1-w}p_{\ctx}(y')^w$.
Differentiating gives
\[
\partial_w\log p_w(y)
=\log\frac{p_{\ctx}(y)}{p_\theta(y)}-A'(w),
\]
and a second derivative
\[
\partial_w^2\log p_w(y)=-A''(w)
=-\Var_{Y\sim p_w}\!\left[\log\frac{p_{\ctx}(Y)}{p_\theta(Y)}\right].
\]
Therefore
\[
R_{\log}''(w)
=\Var_{Y\sim p_w}\!\left[\log\frac{p_{\ctx}(Y)}{p_\theta(Y)}\right].
\]
The bounded-log-density-ratio assumption gives
$\log(p_{\ctx}/p_\theta)\in[-M,M]$, so the variance is at most $(2M)^2$.
Taylor's theorem around the minimizer $w^\star$, where $R_{\log}'(w^\star)=0$,
then yields
\[
R_{\log}(w)-R_{\log}(w^\star)
=\tfrac12 R_{\log}''(\tilde w)(w-w^\star)^2
\le 2M^2(w-w^\star)^2
\]
for some $\tilde w$ between $w$ and $w^\star$.
\end{proof}



\section{Proof of Theorem~2 and the minimax construction}
\label{app:letter-D}

\subsection{Proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:minimax}}
\label{app:thm2}

\subsubsection{Yao-style minimax lower bound}
\label{app:thm2-yao}

We construct two distributions $P_+$ and $P_-$ on
$(q,c,\reli,y^\star)$ that prefer opposite trust decisions and show
that any policy using a fixed trust weight must incur constant excess
risk on some mixture of them.

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.2em]
\item \textbf{$P_+$ (context-correct).} Sample $q$ uniformly from a fixed
support, set $y_\param$ as the model's stale answer, and set
$y_{\ctx}=y^\star$ as the new gold (ConflictBank temporal-update sub-family).
By construction $\reli=1$ on this distribution.
\item \textbf{$P_-$ (context-wrong).} Sample $q$ uniformly, set $y_\param=y^\star$
as the model's correct answer, and set $y_{\ctx}\neq y^\star$ (ConflictBank
misinformation sub-family).  By construction $\reli=0$ on this distribution.
\end{itemize}

Assume the per-family excess risk of a fixed trust value $w$ is lower
bounded by
\[
R(\hat y_w;P_+)-R(\hat y^\star;P_+) \ge \Delta_+(1-w),\qquad
R(\hat y_w;P_-)-R(\hat y^\star;P_-) \ge \Delta_- w,
\]
for some constants $\Delta_+,\Delta_->0$.  This is the formal version of
the statement that under-trusting context is costly on $P_+$, whereas
over-trusting it is costly on $P_-$.

\paragraph{How to instantiate $\Delta_+,\Delta_-$ on a labeled benchmark.}
The constants in \Cref{thm:minimax} are theorem constants, but on a
benchmark with conflict-type annotations they can be estimated directly
from per-sub-family regret slices.  For a sub-family on which context is
the correct source, define
\[
\widehat{\Delta_+}
:=\inf_{w\in[0,1]}
\frac{\widehat R(\hat y_w;P_+)-\widehat R(\hat y^\star;P_+)}{1-w},
\]
and symmetrically, on a sub-family on which the parametric model is the
correct source, define
\[
\widehat{\Delta_-}
:=\inf_{w\in[0,1]}
\frac{\widehat R(\hat y_w;P_-)-\widehat R(\hat y^\star;P_-)}{w}.
\]
These empirical analogues make the T2 construction testable rather than
purely existential: if the estimated gaps stay bounded away from zero,
the fixed-trust lower bound is non-vacuous on the benchmark.  We keep
the main theorem abstract because the precise values depend on the
benchmark taxonomy and on how the sub-family slices are defined.
As an independent confirmation that the failure mode is
sub-family-invariant rather than a quirk of one construction recipe,
the matched-base Llama-3.1-8B GRPO conflict ECE delta survives all
three ConflictBank sub-families separately
(\Cref{tab:grpo-subfamily-survival}).

\begin{table}[H]
\centering\small
\setlength{\tabcolsep}{6pt}
\caption{\textbf{Llama-3.1-8B GRPO conflict-slice ECE delta survives
all three ConflictBank sub-families.}  Same matched-base contrast as
the body, recomputed per sub-family.  All three sub-families
separately exceed the Yao lower bound, demonstrating that the GRPO
overconfidence is not a recipe-specific artifact of any single
ConflictBank construction.}
\label{tab:grpo-subfamily-survival}
\begin{tabular}{lc}
\toprule
\textbf{ConflictBank sub-family} & \textbf{Llama-3.1-8B GRPO conflict $\Delta$ECE}\\
\midrule
Misinformation        & $+0.5722$\\
Temporal-update       & $+0.6902$\\
Semantic-ambiguity    & $+0.6294$\\
\midrule
\emph{Pooled (body \Cref{tab:matched-base-body})} & $+0.264$\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\begin{proof}[Proof of the lower bound in \Cref{thm:minimax}]
Let $w_0\in[0,1]$ and let $P_\lambda=\lambda P_+ + (1-\lambda)P_-$.
Linearity of risk in the data-generating distribution gives
\begin{align}
R(\hat y_{w_0};P_\lambda)-R(\hat y^\star;P_\lambda)
\;&=\;\lambda\!\left[R(\hat y_{w_0};P_+)-R(\hat y^\star;P_+)\right]
\;+\;(1-\lambda)\!\left[R(\hat y_{w_0};P_-)-R(\hat y^\star;P_-)\right]\nonumber\\
\;&\ge\;\lambda\Delta_+(1-w_0)+(1-\lambda)\Delta_-w_0.\nonumber
\end{align}
For $\lambda=\tfrac12$ this becomes
\[
R(\hat y_{w_0};P_{1/2})-R(\hat y^\star;P_{1/2})
\ge \tfrac12\Delta_+(1-w_0)+\tfrac12\Delta_-w_0
\ge \tfrac12\min(\Delta_+,\Delta_-),
\]
so every fixed trust weight incurs constant excess risk on the balanced
mixture.  This proves the non-uniformity claim of
\Cref{thm:minimax}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the construction is realizable in ConflictBank]
\label{rmk:thm2-realizable}
ConflictBank~\citep{su2024conflictbank} contains three sub-families:
temporal-update (context is the new fact), misinformation (context is a
false claim), and semantic-ambiguity.  $P_+$ is realizable as the
temporal-update sub-family; $P_-$ is realizable as the misinformation
sub-family.  The minimax adversary just picks the right sub-family for the
chosen $w_0$.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection{Optional information-theoretic restatement}
\label{app:thm2-fano}

\begin{proposition}[Binary testing restatement]
\label{prop:thm2-fano}
If the active sub-family label is hidden and no auxiliary signal reveals
it, then the minimax excess risk over $\{P_+,P_-\}$ is bounded away from
zero by a binary-testing lower bound.  Equivalently, vanishing
excess risk requires non-trivial mutual information between the observed
signal and the latent reliability regime.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $U\in\{+,-\}$ denote the active sub-family.  When $U$ is not observed,
predicting the optimal trust decision is a binary hypothesis test.  By
standard information-theoretic inequalities, the error of any estimator
of $U$ is bounded below by a positive constant whenever
$I(U;\text{observables})$ is small.  Since choosing the wrong sub-family
incurs at least $\min(\Delta_+,\Delta_-)$ excess risk in the construction
above, the minimax excess risk is also bounded below by a positive
constant.  Thus signal-free policies cannot make the excess risk vanish
over the family.
\end{proof}

\Cref{prop:thm2-fano} is the information-theoretic version of
\Cref{thm:minimax}: if there is no informative signal about reliability,
\emph{any} policy is bottlenecked by the mutual information available.
Empirically, retrieval score, popularity, and contradiction type carry
non-trivial mutual information with $\reli$; the Bayes proxy exploits this,
fixed policies do not.

\subsubsection{Plug-in upper bound for adaptive policies}
\label{app:thm2-upper}

\begin{lemma}[Adaptive plug-in convergence rate]
\label{lem:thm2-upper}
Let $s(q,c)$ be a signal that classifies the sub-family of
\Cref{app:thm2-yao} with error $\varepsilon_s$ (i.e.,
$\PP(s\textup{ predicts wrong sub-family})=\varepsilon_s$).  Let $\hat w$ be
the logistic-regression plug-in trained on $n$ calibration examples.  Then
$R(\hat y_{\hat w};P_{w_0})-R(\hat y^\star;P_{w_0})\leq C\varepsilon_s+O(n^{-1/2})$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Decompose $R(\hat y_{\hat w})-R(\hat y^\star)\leq R(\hat y_{w_s})-R(\hat y^\star)+R(\hat y_{\hat w})-R(\hat y_{w_s})$,
where $w_s\in\{0,1\}$ is the optimal hard-threshold weight given $s$.  The
first term is bounded by the classification error $\varepsilon_s$ times the
sub-family loss gap.  The second term is bounded by
\Cref{lem:excess-risk-zero-one} applied to $\hat w$, which is
$O(n^{-1/2})$ by standard logistic-regression consistency.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Signal separability controls the adaptive gap]
\label{prop:t2-separability}
Let $U\in\{+,-\}$ denote the active sub-family under the balanced mixture
$P_{1/2}=\tfrac12 P_+ + \tfrac12 P_-$.  Define the Bayes sub-family error
from signal $s$ by
\[
\varepsilon_s:=\inf_{h:\mathcal{S}\to\{+,-\}} \PP\!\left[h(s(q,c))\neq U\right].
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[leftmargin=1.4em,itemsep=2pt]
\item for every $s$-measurable trust policy $w(s)\in[0,1]$,
\[
R(\hat y_{w(s)};P_{1/2})-R(\hat y^\star;P_{1/2})
\;\ge\;\frac{\Delta_{\min}}{2}\,\varepsilon_s,
\qquad
\Delta_{\min}:=\min(\Delta_+,\Delta_-);
\]
\item the adaptive plug-in of \Cref{lem:thm2-upper} satisfies
\[
R(\hat y_{\hat w};P_{1/2})-R(\hat y^\star;P_{1/2})
\;\le\; C\,\varepsilon_s + O(n^{-1/2}).
\]
\end{enumerate}
Hence the adaptive-vs-fixed separation is controlled sharply, up to
constants, by the signal-separability parameter $\varepsilon_s$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $w(s)$ be any measurable policy and define the induced regime
classifier $h_w(s):=\one{w(s)\ge 1/2}\in\{0,1\}$, identified with
$\{+,-\}$.  On $P_+$, whenever $h_w(s)=-$ we have $w(s)<1/2$, so
\[
R(\hat y_{w(s)};P_+)-R(\hat y^\star;P_+)\ge \Delta_+(1-w(s))\ge \Delta_+/2.
\]
Similarly, on $P_-$, whenever $h_w(s)=+$ we have $w(s)\ge 1/2$, so
\[
R(\hat y_{w(s)};P_-)-R(\hat y^\star;P_-)\ge \Delta_-w(s)\ge \Delta_-/2.
\]
Averaging over the balanced mixture gives
\[
R(\hat y_{w(s)};P_{1/2})-R(\hat y^\star;P_{1/2})
\ge \frac{\Delta_{\min}}{2}\,\PP[h_w(s)\neq U]
\ge \frac{\Delta_{\min}}{2}\,\varepsilon_s,
\]
since $\varepsilon_s$ is the minimal classification error achievable from
$s$.  The upper bound is exactly \Cref{lem:thm2-upper} specialized to
$P_{1/2}$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Supplementary derivations: Fano sharpening}
\label{app:fano-sharpening}

On the two-subfamily construction of \Cref{app:thm2-yao}, Le Cam's
two-point method is cleaner than Fano because the latent regime is
binary.

\begin{proposition}[Two-point lower bound for hidden reliability regimes]
\label{prop:lecam-thm2}
Let $U\in\{+,-\}$ index the active sub-family with prior
$\PP(U=+)=\PP(U=-)=1/2$, and let $P_+,P_-$ denote the resulting
observable distributions.  Then any estimator $\hat U$ satisfies
\[
\inf_{\hat U}\PP(\hat U\neq U)\;\ge\;\frac{1-\TV(P_+,P_-)}{2}.
\]
If choosing the wrong regime incurs excess risk at least
$\Delta_{\min}:=\min(\Delta_+,\Delta_-)$, then every policy has minimax
excess risk at least
\[
\frac{\Delta_{\min}}{2}\bigl(1-\TV(P_+,P_-)\bigr).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The testing bound is the standard Le Cam inequality
\citep[Lemma~2.2]{tsybakov2009nonparametric}.  The second claim follows
because, under the T2 construction, a policy that mistakes the active
regime necessarily pays at least $\Delta_{\min}$ excess risk.
\end{proof}

\Cref{prop:lecam-thm2} is the sharp binary analogue of the Fano-style
statement in \Cref{prop:thm2-fano}.  It makes explicit that the problem
is easy only when the observables nearly identify the hidden reliability
regime, i.e., when $\TV(P_+,P_-)\approx 1$.


\subsection{Worked example of the minimax construction}
\label{app:worked-minimax}

For concreteness, fix the conflict subset to be a binary classification
problem with two answers $\{A,B\}$.  Let $D_+$ be the distribution where
$y_{\param}=A,y_{\ctx}=B,y^\star=B$ (context-correct); let $D_-$ be
the distribution where $y_{\param}=A,y_{\ctx}=B,y^\star=A$
(context-wrong).  Both have $y_{\param}\neq y_{\ctx}$, so they live on
the conflict subset.  By construction $\reli=1$ on $D_+$ and $\reli=0$
on $D_-$.

For any fixed weight $w_0\in[0,1]$, the policy $\hat y_{w_0}$ chooses
$B$ if $w_0\geq 1/2$ and $A$ if $w_0<1/2$.  On the mixture
$P_{1/2} = \tfrac12 D_+ + \tfrac12 D_-$:
\begin{itemize}
\item if $w_0 \geq 1/2$: the policy always chooses $B$, so it is correct on
the $D_+$ half and wrong on the $D_-$ half, for error $1/2$
\item if $w_0 < 1/2$: the policy always chooses $A$, so it is correct on
the $D_-$ half and wrong on the $D_+$ half, again for error $1/2$
\end{itemize}
Thus every fixed-weight policy has error $1/2$ on the balanced mixture,
whereas a signal-adaptive policy that identifies the active sub-family
achieves error $0$.  This is the simplest concrete witness for
\Cref{thm:minimax}: the gap is not asymptotic or stylistic, it is a
literal factor-of-two decision error on the balanced conflict mixture.



\section{Proof of Theorem~3, assumption audits, and multilingual evidence}
\label{app:letter-E}

\subsection{Proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:eta-bayes}}
\label{app:thm3}

\subsubsection{Setup and the $\eta$-generalized posterior}
\label{app:thm3-setup}

We adopt the generalized Bayes update of \citet{bissiri2016}.  Let
$\mathcal{M}=\{q_\xi:\xi\in\Xi\}$ be a model family of distributions over
$\Y$ (in the LLM setting, $q_\xi$ is the implicit answer distribution after
some reasoning prefix; $\xi$ encodes that prefix).  The
$\eta$-generalized posterior given a single piece of evidence
$z\sim P_z$ is
\begin{equation}
\pi_\eta(\xi\mid z)\;\propto\;\pi(\xi)\,\exp\!\left(-\eta\,\ell(z;\xi)\right),
\qquad \ell(z;\xi)\,=\,-\log q_\xi(z).
\label{eq:gen-bayes-app}
\end{equation}
For $\eta=1$ and well-specified $\mathcal{M}$, this is the ordinary Bayes
posterior.  For misspecified $\mathcal{M}$,
\citet{grunwald2017} prove that there is a critical safe rate
$\bar\eta\in(0,1]$ such that for $\eta>\bar\eta$ the iterated posterior
hypercompresses---it places more mass on KL-bad models than the predictive.

In the LLM CoT setting, $z_t$ is the $t$-th reasoning segment, sampled
\emph{by the same model} from $p_t(z\mid q,c,z_{1:t-1})$.  This is endogenous
evidence.  The Berk--Nash literature~\citep{esponda2016,fudenberg2021}
studies exactly this case and gives a fixed-point characterization.

\subsubsection{The safe-rate lemma}
\label{app:thm3-shrinks}

\begin{lemma}[Larger projection distance implies smaller safe rate]
\label{lem:eta-bar-monotone}
Let $\xi^\star$ be the KL projection of the truth $\PP^\star$ onto
$\mathcal{M}$, and let $D^\star=\KL(\PP^\star\|q_{\xi^\star})$ be the
projection's KL distance.  Then the Gr\"unwald--van~Ommen safe rate
$\bar\eta$ for the family $\mathcal{M}$ satisfies
\[
\bar\eta\leq c_{|\Y|,\pi}/D^\star
\]
for a finite-alphabet constant $c_{|\Y|,\pi}$ depending on the
bracketing entropy and the prior.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
This is the safe-rate bound of \citet[Theorem~1.6]{grunwald2017}, which
states $\bar\eta\leq c/D^\star$ where $c$ is determined by the model
family's bracketing entropy and the prior.  Because $\Y$ is finite in our
setting, we can make the dependence explicit as $c_{|\Y|,\pi}$; see
\Cref{app:thm3-shrinks-explicit} below.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Explicit constant on finite $\Y$.}
\label{app:thm3-shrinks-explicit}
On a finite output space $\Y$ the bracketing entropy of any
sub-family of $\Delta(\Y)$ is finite at every fixed scale.  A standard
simplex discretization gives
\[
\log N_{[]}(\varepsilon,\Delta(\Y),\|\cdot\|_2)
\;\le\;(|\Y|-1)\log\frac{3}{\varepsilon},
\]
so the entropy integral in the Gr\"unwald--van~Ommen bound is finite and
depends only on $|\Y|$.  If the prior puts positive local mass around the
KL projection, that dependence can be bundled into a finite constant
$c_{|\Y|,\pi}$, giving exactly the form used in
\Cref{lem:eta-bar-monotone}.  We use this specialization only to make the
dimension/prior dependence explicit; the paper's arguments remain
qualitative in that they use only the monotonicity
$\bar\eta\propto 1/D^\star$ up to this finite prefactor.

\subsubsection{Reduction to Berk--Nash dynamics: proof of Proposition~\ref{prop:berk-nash-reduction}}
\label{app:berk-nash-reduction}

The previous version of this paper carried a ``structural analogy''
caveat asserting that the Berk--Nash language was suggestive rather
than literal because the model family
$\mathcal{M}$ induced by reasoning prefixes is not parametric in
the strict sense of \citet{esponda2016,fudenberg2021}.  This
subsection removes that caveat by giving a literal reduction; the
key observation is that the reduction does not require parametric
$\mathcal{M}$, only continuity of the expected-update operator on
the answer simplex $\Delta(\Y)$.

\begin{definition}[Auxiliary Berk--Nash game $G_{q,c,\eta}$]
\label{def:bn-game}
